--- 帖子 #1 ---
Hi,

First off, I am a full-time trader and I have been trading in the currency market for more than four years now. As a long time lurker of this forum, I finally feel the need to participate in forums, as day-trading has gotten pretty boring. I have three very powerful strategies in my trading arsenal, and what better way to start than to share one of the strategies here. I wouldn’t call this an entirely mechanical system, as you need to use some discretion. I will be outlining some of the important factors that may need consideration before entering a trade based on this system, later in this post.

I call this system: A.M.G Waves

Timeframe: Any. But, I use 1Hr or higher to avoid whipsaws.
Pair: Any Currency Pair.
Indicator(s):
Stochastic Oscillator (8,3,3)
5 SMA

Before I give out the entry requirements, please take a look at the following picture. A setup only exists where the fib retracement of an impulse wave is 61.8 or 78.6. The idea behind this method is that provided AB wave retraces by 61.8% or 78.6%, it should equal the CD wave. Only look for setups that are in the direction of the bigger trend (ie: If you are looking at setups on the hourly, then only look for signals that are with the daily trend).

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

{chart 1}

Long
Generally, you are buying in an uptrend, when the AB impulse wave retraces to the 61.8 or 78.6 level. Before pinpointing a precise entry, you wait for the next candle (confirmation candle) to form. This must not exceed the low made by the retracement and has to be a bullish reversal candle (ie, Harami, Doji, Bullish Maribozu, Bullish Belt hold, etc).

At the precise entry point:

1) The new candle following the Confirmation Candle is on or near the 5 SMA.
2) On the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking up. This cross should not happen in the overbought region (80 or above).

Short
Generally, you are selling in a downtrend, when the AB impulse wave retraces to the 61.8 or 78.6 level. Before pinpointing a precise entry, you wait for the next candle (confirmation candle) to form. This must not exceed the high made by the retracement and has to be a bearish reversal candle (ie, Harami, Doji, Bearish Maribozu, Bearish Belt hold, etc).

At the precise entry point:

1) The new candle following the Confirmation Candle is on or near the 5 SMA.
2) On the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking down. This cross should not happen in the oversold region (20 or below).

INVALID SETUPS

A setup is considered invalid:

1) If there is a news release within 15-30mins.
2) If the confirmation candle moves so much that the stop loss is widened to a point where the Risk/Reward ratio is no longer 1:1.5.
3) If there is a major psychological support/resistance (ie, 2.0000 for Cable, 1.5000 for EURUSD, etc) before the first profit level (Target 1).
4) If the setup is against the major trend (atleast two TFs up from the one you are trading with).

STOP LOSS

Stop Loss should be placed where the first impulse wave starts (Point C on the charts). Only take a trade if the stop loss is smaller than your
projected Target 2.

ENTRY STRATEGY

Here is an example, using a $10,000 account at 1:100 leverage.
I am only willing to risk 1% of my account and assume the stop loss has already been establish (start of the first impulse wave) and is 30pips + 3pips spread.

(10,000*0.01) / 33 = 3

So, I can trade at $3/pip, meaning I can go into the trade with 3 mini lots. There are three profit taking levels, so I should divide the lots into three equal lots and enter all of them at the same price (entry point). In this case, I have 3 x 1mini lots to enter at the same price and I will exit each mini lot at the different target levels, if they are not stopped out first.

EXIT STRATEGY

Carrying on from the previous example, I would exit my first lot at Target 1. If price does reach Target 2, I will take out the second lot, and move my stop loss to Break Even (Entry point). I will then take out my last lot when Target 3 is reached.

If you look at the charts provided, you can see that the targets can be calculated using the Fibonacci Expansion tool.

-When the confirmation candle is a Harami (Inside bar), use FE 50.0 as Target 1, FE 61.8 as Target 2 and FE 78.6 as Target 3.

-When the 'AB' wave consists of more than 10 candles, use FE 50.0 as Target 1, FE 61.8 as Target 2 and FE 78.6 as Target 3.

-When the confirmation candle is quite large, use FE 61.8 as Target 1, FE 78.6 as Target 2 and FE 100.0 as Target 3.

Illustration

Please take a look at the following charts for examples of Short and Long trades that I took recently. I will add more upon request.

Question- The biggest problem I've had with fibs is choosing the swing points to anchor them to. How do you choose your swing highs and lows?  You can almost always find one that will give you whatever retrace you're looking for.  Also, how close does price have to come to one of your retrace points before you consider it a hit?

--- 帖子 #5 ---
Well you are right in that people can interpret fibs in different ways (intraday swings, session swings, wave swings). But I always look at wave swings as I have found them to be the most effective. Please take a look at the charts I posted to see how I draw fibs. And as for price, it depends on how big the wave is. If its 4-10 candles long, then you want price to test and close below/above the fib level. However, if its a larger wave, then as long is it is about 7pips near the fib level, it can be considered a valid retrace.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #11 ---
Its not only 61.8, but also 78.6 fib retracement level. From my testing during the development stages of this system (7 months ago), I found out that the strong trend continuations do retrace 38% and 50%, but that is when you take the swing points of the entire trend and for my method to work, you take the swing points of the last impulsive wave. Please refer to the charts I have posted. I would gladly post more, if you need clarification.

Thanks

Okay, here are some recent trades. AB is an impulse wave with recognisable swing points. Please refer to {chart 1} on my first post where you can see how a wave is always followed by a retracement. So your Point A in a downtrend would be the first Swing High after a retrace. Point B would be the immediate Swing Low (as intraday traders you should look for waves consisting of 4-10 1Hr candles).

--- 帖子 #25 ---
I will try to answer to this question, as it is a problem for me as well to determine the correct impulsive wave. But I tried to re-read everything Daz said here and he actually stated very clear how to catch the last impuslive wave.

First of all, you look at Daily. Lets take GY. Even yesterday wasa bullish day, this doesnt mean that the trend is up - it is obviously down, even a child can guess that. So we trade on the short side only.

Then we move to 1H or 4H timeframe, depending on your taste.You look at the chart, and try to spot the last swing high , i.e. the last peak the price made before falling again. This is your point A. Then you look for the swing low (it should be only one swing low, coz if there are 2 or more, it means you didnt determine the correct swing high). The last swing low is where the price start to turn up. This is your point B. Now you pull the Fibs from A to B and wait for the price to come close to 61 or 78 level.

And from here you know what to do. Hope I cleared something for you.

This is a trade I got in today for GY, and Im still in, as I am waiting for the 61 extension to be hit. It is a good trade, thank you Daz.

I love this method because it reminds me of the basics of trading I used to read when I started my forex journey, and still I didnt know how to properly implement them. Now these tools make sense together.

Cheers.

--- 帖子 #65 ---
Hi,

5SMA is used to give you a better entry, as price usually retraces to this level. It is not used as a confirmation for entry, only to give you the best RISK/REWARD trade.

For example, in a short trade setup, you will see the confirmation candle (next candle after the retracement candle[Point C]) breaking the 5SMA on the downside. The next candle (entry candle) would normally go back up to test the 5SMA. Your precise entry would be when the candle is on the 5SMA, or even better if it goes above the 5SMA. Ofcourse, sometimes it may not even retrace to the 5SMA and continue going down. In these cases, just wait until you are a few pips away from the 5SMA as price usually hovers up and down before it pick up the downward momentum. Ofcourse, if you feel price has gotten too far away from the 5SMA (hence making the Stop too wide), just look for another setup.

Usually, if you see a setup in USDJPY, you will see similar setups throughout the Yen pairs, and so, you can take the best setup (Best RISK/REWARD trade).

Thanks

--- 帖子 #77 ---
To enter fib levels, you right click on the dotted lines, and go to 'properties'. There you enter the levels you want. 0.50, 0.618, 0.786 & 1.000. And in the description field, just add FE 0.50, etc.

If you are talking about the blue lines below the candles, don't worry, that is just for illustration.

Hope this helps.

Thanks

--- 帖子 #102 ---
Hi Eagle Eye,

Thanks for the response. Firstly, you use Fibonacci Expansion (Point A, B, C) to get the targets. Secondly, you identify the trend on the longer term time frame by simply looking at the waves (ie: Higher highs and higher lows in uptrend). Also, you could trade on the hourly timeframe when price is in a corrective phase on the daily.

Finally, the reason you only found a few trades is because your swing points are very far away from each other. If you look at my examples, you will see that impulsive waves are usually 4-10 candles long. If they are longer than this, usually, you will have that setup on a higher timeframe.

Hope this helps.

Thanks

--- 帖子 #118 ---
Point A is a swing point (retracement point of the previous impulse wave). Please take a look at the first chart in my initial post. In a downtrend, Point A is a swing high (a higher high than the previous candle and the candle after).

You can have more than one setup per day on any one pair, But when I reach my target for the day, I don't trade.

And yes to trading  on the 15min TF. Just need to know that the success rate declines as you go into lower TFs, but you do get more setups. Just keep your AB waves small (4-10 candles)

I hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #203 ---
The key Fib Expansion levels are FE 50, FE 61.8, FE 78.6 and FE 100

Mostly, I follow the Exit Strategy outlined in my first post. So, I split my position into 3 and take out my first one at FE 50 (if it is larger than the amount I risked) otherwise, at FE 61.8. I will take out the second position at the next FE level and move my stop to B/E. THe last lot will be taken off at the 3rd  FE level.

To answer your question, the second target is FE 61.8 = 0.7882

--- 帖子 #215 ---
DazFX, great system, beautiful in its simplicity. Great to see that exit is also being addressed in such unambiguous fashion. Many thanks for sharing.

A few questions, if I may (in blue typeface):

[Edit] Q5. Could you give a ballpark idea as to what percentage of trades have been winners? (By a win, I mean a net positive gain across all three components of a trade).

--- 帖子 #216 ---
Hi David,

Its 12:33am here in the UK, but I will try my best to answer your questions.

1) The ideal setup is when the levels are touched to the pip, or when they are tested (candle close inside the levels). Then you have the setups where the candle is a few pips short of the levels. If you keep your AB waves short (4-10 candles) by moving to the appropriate TFs, you will be surprised at how often price respects these levels, especially when its moving with the longer term trend. Price could go beyond 78.6, but it should close below the level.

2) Yes, the hook up/down should happen either in the Confirmation Candle or the Entry Candle.

3) Looking back at my initial post, I can see I haven't made it very clear. Its Target 3.

4) When I first came up with this strategy, I moved stop to b/e upon hitting target 1. The problem with that is price will hit my entry point and continue moving in my direction taking out the other targets. This happens much frequently than price reversing at target 1.

5) 15/20 winning trades.  3/20 hit stop.   2/20 hit stop after hitting Target 1. All based on trades taken on the hourly time frame and mostly following the rules.

As you quite nicely said, this is just a ballpark idea, I don't want to mislead anyone.

Having said all this, the Entry, Exit rules are what I follow (My emotions do get the better of me sometimes) and not a requirement for this system to work effectively. I am sure there are better entry/exit strategies out there.

I hope I have answered your questions to your satisfaction.

-DAZ-

--- 帖子 #298 ---
No, I am suggesting only to move to a larger timeframe when the waves are too big. (ie, an AB wave with 20 candles on the hourly, will only be a wave with 5 candles on the 4Hr chart, and hence, you look for the entry signal on the 4hr.)

This is because, the waves are more accurate when they are small. Also remember, the length of time it takes AB to form is roughly how long it takes CD to form.

EDIT: The USDCHF is fully closed, just waiting for Target 3 on Cable. I think I will call it a day after this. Didn't expect to reach my daily target already. I will still look for setups and report here.

--- 帖子 #303 ---
Hi AT,

Yes, you have got the hang of it. Remember, when looking to short, either you enter on the 5SMA or even better, enter slightly higher (as the higher it goes, the tighter the stop loss gets). I was watching the 5-15mins charts on the entry candle, and placed a limit order at a round figure (open of previous 15min candle) and luckily it was hit before price went down.

EDIT: Cable Target 3 (1.9842) HIT!! Notice how price bounces off these Fib Expansion levels. Entry higher than 5SMA, as price is always likely to test the Daily Pivot.

--- 帖子 #369 ---
You got synchronous communication compared to asynchronous here. Synchronous means basically chat, e.g. you don't wait for the answer. Asynchronous is for example e-mail, forum, etc. In a rapid changing environment like forex, sometimes minutes or even seconds make the difference.

--- 帖子 #409 ---

--- 帖子 #410 ---
I see some people are having trouble seting up a fib tool, hope this will help.

Right click the fib tool button - CUSTOMIZE - in the "available" list click on Fibonacci Expansion and - INSERT -. Now you have your tool available straight from main platform window.

Fibo properties:

Level    Description

1          100%  %$ (you actualy don't need this one)

0.786    78.6% %$

0.618    61.8   %$

Fibo Expansion properties:

Level    Description

0.5       T1 50%  %$

0.618    T2 61.8%  %$

0.786    T3 78.6%   %$

I did some research on divergences and in an up trend they compare the highs of the price to the highs of the oscillator to seek divergence.  We don't have that here, the highs match so we can say the up trend is still valid, plus we are now oversold so possible uptrend to come from that perspective too.

--- 帖子 #592 ---
OK, I have found out that the reason th MFT_Stoch didn't look like the 4Hr close/close.

ChowClown is correct in that using 32,12,12 on a 1Hr chart gives a better approximation to 8,3,3 on a 4Hr chart than does 32,3,3.

However there is a problem with using 4Hr charts or an MTF_stoch set for a 4Hr periond on a 1 hr chart. The problem is that ther are up to 4 possible 4Hr charts (due to the local time used for the chart) e.g. GMT, GMT+1, GMT+2, GMT+3 etc. I hate 4Hr charts for this reason, but it is much worse when you use a 4hr chart with an indicator which only uses the open or close (not so bad if it uses high and Low as well).

I think that this is the reason why somewhere on either Spudfyre's or TEB's thread, somebody suggested using 32,3,3 as a longer term confirmation of an 8,3,3.

It is interesting that althoug I have often seem systems using 5,3,3 or 8,3,3 or even 14,3,3, it is only the first parameter which has been changed - the %D and Smoothing always seem to be kept at 3.

I attach the MTF_Stoch indicator should anybody want to use it. Note that for this Dazfx system, from what I understand, you would place it on a 1hr chart and set the following:

Timeframe = 240 i.e. minutes

Kperiod = 8

MAMethod = 1      0=SMA, 1=EMA

Price = 1              0 = High/Low, 1= Close/Close

I hope this helps,

Ian

According to the rule, the cross must not happen in the OB or OS area.... join us in the tradingroom and see how we trade live

--- 帖子 #609 ---
Sup mate,

-------------------

Short

2) On the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking down. This cross should not happen in the oversold region (20 or below).

Long

2) On the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking up. This cross should not happen in the overbought region (80 or above).

-------------------

The above excerpt from the first post doesn't say 'No Hooks in OB and OS area'. Instead it says no cross in the OB region for Long, and no cross in the OS region for Short.

Then again, that is how I interpreted the initial post.

--- 帖子 #610 ---
As I understand it, I believe that the cross should not happen in the OB for long trade and in the OS for sell trade.  Just use the common sense, if it is already overbought, then there is no reason for people to buy it anymore, ( that is why they use the word overbought).  So it is a good signal for sell. And as I understand it, if you have a short setup and if stoch cross in the OB region , it is good to go in. The reverse is for OS with long setup.

correct me if I am wrong

--- 帖子 #623 ---
Hi Getright,

The Fib extension tool is not a special indicator, it is provided on almost all platforms  and charting packages. If you are using Metatrader, it is on the tool bar. Th icon for it is three parallel dotted lines,  with an upside down 'hockey stick ' and the letter F.

To use it click on it, then click on the oldest point oyou want to draw from, then click on the maximum of the pullback. This will then display two dotted lines, click anywher on the lines to select the tool  - this will show white dots on the lines. You can then click on a white dot and move the line where you want it.

--- 帖子 #625 ---
Hi Birdy,

To put the price on Fib retrace,ment or Fib expansion levels, you :

1. Click on the Fib line to select it.

2). Left click and then select Expansion Properties (say)

3). Go to tab Fibo Levels

4. Edit the Description filed of a level entry, after the description insert ' %$' but without the quotes.

Note that you can also add in new levels if you so wish by clicking on  the ADD.

5. The just click OK to finish and it is done - the Fib will show your modifications.

5

--- 帖子 #634 ---
Hi Daz,

I just found this thread yesterday.  I'm a long time user of Fibs.  Your system is similar to DiNapoli's work in many ways.  He also uses multiple fib targets with great success.

I'd like to contribute a few of things, if you don't mind.

Try putting up the 88.6 Fib Retracement.  You'll find that those overshoots on the 78.6 are hitting the 88.6 to the pip.  The great majority of the time it'll be the wick that hits it, it's rare for the close to hit it.  In fact, it it closes at the 88.6, you're going to see it continue on it's way to the 100 retracement more often than not.

Different pairs have different characteristics when it comes to fibs.  For example, the GBP will hit the 127.2 expansion quite often while the Eur tends to turn around at the 100 expansion.  I imagine you've internalized this already.  For others, they should keep records of what pair does what, it is valuable information.

Finally, Fibs work across time as well.  You state that you prefer 4-10 bars for your setups.  The fib numbers of 5, 8, and 13 are worth looking at.  So that a retracement that seems to terminate on the 5th bar is probably the one.  However, I wouldn't bet any money just on this alone, but it's a nice addition to the confluence of events that lead to a setup.

Look at today's Eur hourly.  The high of 6018 to the low of 5968 is 8 bars, not counting the initial bar.  Then the next high 5997 is 3 bars, not counting the initial bar (and 3 is a fib number). The very next bar made the same high and then turned bearish.

Great work.

--- 帖子 #643 ---
Hi Marvostica,

1) You get CD when you plott the Fib Expansion from AB to C. Remember you're trading the CD wave (entry near C and exit near or at D).

2) FE is from A to B to C.

3) Important exit levels: FE 50.0, FE 61.8, FE 78.6 & FE 100.0

FE 50.0 is your 1st Target if Stop Loss to Entry is lower than Entry to FE 50.0. Otherwise, 1st Target is FE 61.8. Keep taking out your positions as you reach the higher FE levels.

Thanks

--- 帖子 #673 ---
Hi,

Use the Fib expansion tool under Insert>Fibonacci menu.

Its like the letter "V".

You place the left node at A, middle node at B and the right node at C.

It would give the extensions.

Hope this helps.

Peace

I just would like oppionions from people who have been trading this method and watching it through news events.

--- 帖子 #685 ---
I normally let it ride if my I am in profit by say 20pips or more. Otherwise, I close the trade when it nears news time and price gets erratic. Although I let the trade run, I watch it carefully, and if I see the news was against me, and price is also moving against, I will simply close the trade with a few pips profit. Sometimes, I have locked in Target 1/2, at these times, I just let the trade run as my S/L would be at Break Even, so I won't be losing anything.

Hopefully, this should help clear some doubts.

--- 帖子 #749 ---
hi Syahmi, Am new to this system, to get the fib, go to insert on MT4, go down to fibonacci and there u see retracement. Try and locate swing high and low and plot the fib on it to get the retrace. Then go back to the same insert, fibonacci and there u pick up expansion.plot it on the chart to give u the targets lines. the retracement shd give AB While expansion shd give ABC. Never mind all those diff forms of fibs u are seeing else u confuse yourself. u must be able to determine the trend which has been the headache of many traders. As for me i hope to start making money using this great system.I have been able to spot some trades today UChf 1Hr,let see how UJ 4Hr goes, so i wish myself good luck and u too. Nerry.

--- 帖子 #763 ---
Hello Nerry, the stoch setting is 833, the normal stoch setting. plz read the first post by daz for good understanding of the system. anyway, u risk 1% size of your acct, and split that into three trades. the first trade as its tgt set to tgt1 while the second trade has its set to tgt2. once tgt2 is met, u set the sl of trade 3 to b/e and let tgt 3 be met.

LOOK for possible trade on GCHF and EURGBP on 4hrs during asian session. I can see retracement on them now for possible trade continuation. the close of today's candle will give better idea.

--- 帖子 #780 ---
Can anyone tell me how I can get the Fibonacci Retracements and Expansions to show price as well. (On the first page, last post, Daz has a graph that show retracement level @ price. and FE level @ price. How can I get that to show?

--- 帖子 #781 ---
Double click on your mt4 fib tool to get to its properties, then enter the following at the end of a description level:

@ %$

For example I have mine to display the following description at (1, 0.786, and 0.618 fib levels).

Swing Start (0.0) > %$

Stop Loss Zone (78.6) > %$

Entry Zone (61.8) > %$

--- 帖子 #809 ---
Hi!

Your system looks simple and powerfull, i like to attach some ideas

1., the power of the system multiplied by a big factor because nearly all cases on the chart you can see a forming cup and handle (or reverse cup and handle) when the forming CD line reached the point B, and as you take position at point C, you are overtaking the market, and getting early into position

2., as this is a discretional system, automatic backtesting is impossible

3., maybe for some beginners it's hard to find the correct AB impulsive waves, or the trend direction, don't wonder on this. When i was a beginner, it was hard to find the trend direction, currently i just blink one on the chart, and one on the higher timeframe, and i see the direction. so they need to practise more and more, if you can't find the correct AB line, or the correct trend direction, then you have to avoid trading, because your basic skills need to sharpen.

4., i like to find longer AB lines (longer means more bars), because on shorter lines the wick of the candle is very confusing, when it's breaking the fibo lines, and hard to decide to open position or not.

--- 帖子 #875 ---
Hello all,

I will give an explanation of the attached chart. You will notice the ABC wave formation that we all know and look for. Near C and rebounding off the FIB50 is a shooting star or pin candle which is the reversal and 3 candles later the black down candle that closes below SMA5.

The FIB is colour coded and you can see % marked on it. I normally have those as price levels but for the exercise have changed them. The FIB levels 21.4 & 14 are actually the 78.6 & 86 retracement and the 38.2 & 61.8 should really be the other way around but it does not matter. The idea is that if there is a retracement to a blue level the extension will be to a blue level (+10 pips for short, -10 for long), pink to pink, orange to orange. I use basically the same SL as the DAZFX method, but PT1 for me is 1.5 x risk and PT2 IS 2 X RISK or the coloured extension, whichever comes first. I am looking at maybe going to 1:1 for PT1 and 2:1 or FIB level for PT2.

You will notice the RSI 14. I have been experimenting with it as confirmation. It appears (still to be further tested) that if it bounces or rebounds or breaks through the 50 level the entry signal is a bit more reliable.

To set these FIBS on Dealbook, you go into properties and set 0 - red, 14 - pink, 21.4 - orange, 38.2 - blue, 50 - blue, 61.8 - blue, 100 - red, 118 - pink, 127 - orange, 161.8 - blue.

Not sure how to get the same set up on MT4 as I have only just started using it.

All in all, not a lot different to DAZFX. I also throw in the red EMA 25, as you can see it quite often bounces of it.

To put the FIB on the chart pull from your B to your A.

Feel free to add any observations, criticisms etc.

Regards.

--- 帖子 #904 ---
Market Phases

There are only three ways the market can go; Up  Down  Sideways With the swing high/low definition now in mind we can start to build some layers on to the chart to identify these market phases and start to do a simple count of these swing highs and lows.

In short  The market is going up when price is making higher highs and higher lows  The market is going down when price is making lower highs and lower lows  The market is going sideways when price is not making higher highs and higher lows OR lower highs lower lows This may sound like child's play and a statement of the obvious but you will be surprised at how often people will forget these simple facts. One of the biggest questions I get asked is, which way is it a market going? By doing a simple exercise you can see which way that price is going and decide on your trading plan and more importantly timing of a trade.
What do I mean by timing? It may be that you are looking for a shorting opportunity as the overall trend is down but price on your entry time frame is still going up (making HH's & HL's).  There is, at this stage, no point in trying to short a rising market until price action start to point down (making LH's & LL's. More on this shortly).

and i hope am not boring with this

--- 帖子 #931 ---
Let me say this, setup with 20 candles or more works but setup with 4-10 candles work best.

if u read very well, this method aims at picking the recent impulse wave, that is recent swing hi/lo and not the whole large impulse wave. if u read very well, the large impulve waves retraces to 38.2 to 50.0 most times which indicate strong wave/trend but this system takes advantage of the recent wave pull back to our defined fib ratio for possible trade.

so my advice is this, if u get a large wave and feel like trading, go to 4hrs and see if the wave its a reflection of swing hi-lo

anyway, let's meet in the tradingroom for more

Mike

A lot of us at times have difficulty recognizing the direction of a trend. I have posted 2 charts and maybe my explanation might help some people with this difficult concept. If you look at the 1st chart where I have zoomed in and indicated a possible entry point you can see it might have returned a 1:1 profit and maybe more if you hung on long enough. I see it as risky because I think the trend is undecided by virtue of the red (25) and green (50) ema's closing up and flattening out along with the price ranging. If you look at the second chart the profit potential is far greater, the trend is more defined. They are the same chart a few days apart. The second one clearly has the ema's down and I think is a much lower risk option.

I only illustrate this for the purpose of saying that by zooming out and getting a bigger picture, you may get a better perspective, not to suggest it is a perfect setup for a trade. It is purely to demonstrate the bigger picture.

I think we need to learn to be patient and wait for established trends. There are enough currencies to choose from to be patient.

I welcome any comments.

Hi guys:

re: CHF and AUD trades.

CHF worked, hit all targets

AUD did not (I never entered). This pair can give some very nice impulse moves. So if you are looking to expand your pair universe, give Mathilda a spin on the foor. But be warned, she can turn on a dime, as seen. So R:R, money management and appropriate stops will be a key.

-------------------------------

Also, in response to questions about identifying trends, I toss the simple idea of Trend Channels into the hat. I find it easy to use, and gives a handy visual representation of the trend on your time frame, whether you expand or contract your chart. Plus it has the added bonus of identifying possible trade set-ups/exits at the outer lines (or possibly the middle lines as well), which are just trend lines after all.

Here is an example. The first chart is a scrunched up 60m AUD to show the required swing points. It is suggesting a bottom might be rounding into form over the past 5 trading sessions. See the series of higher lows. The second is the same chart expanded. It shows how easy it is to see the trend in the background even once the detail is blown up. The second chart also shows how a TC can help identify a potential trade set-up. I dont know if this trade will be a good one (do we ever?) as it is a countertrend to the major downtrend of the last 6 weeks in this pair. However, the method is solid and repeats itself over and over, whenever you have swing highs and lows. You will find the same is true on suggesting exit or reversal points. If you already employ trend lines in your analysis, this is a helpful adjunct.

Anways, just a humble suggestion of one simple way to sometimes manage the issue of identifying trend that also has the added benefit of alerting you to possible entry and exit spots.

edit: i later noticed i neglected to add the fibs to this chart on the right. Hopefully its not too difficult to visualize where they would be. Entry near the 78% level. Sorry about that. The trade is still going after a downside challenge to the 8650 levels.

--- 帖子 #971 ---
Here is one more example of a trend channel

recent EUR chart

You can see how the upper line held price, before a 200+ pip move south.

You can trade either direction with a TC. But obviously a short will always offer more pips with a downtrending channel while a long will offer more with an uptrending TC.

Can work very well with the DAZ method.

One more comment on using a trend channel with this method.

Using the same AUD chart from 8/18, a TC might had helped you fine tune the targets by showing where to look for strong support -- at the lower leg of the upsloping trend channel.

Had you been looking short at the 50 fib near the 00 level (which would not have been completely unreasonable given the strong intermediate term downtrend), the TC was suggesting possible stop levels and/or adjustments that could be made to the normal DAZ targets.  Here the 1H candle was an OB not an IB, but the overall idea is still valid either way.  Or perhaps kept you out of the trade all together as entering a short into strong support is not always a great strategy. Still, there were some short-term pips there for the taking. Maybe moving to a lower TF would have been the thing to do?

Anyways, just an idea to throw out for considerartion.

Hi folks:

Here is an updated 240m EUR chart referenced a few posts above. The trend channel did hold at the 4800 + 50 fib level, and there was a short there for 50 pips or more, depending on how aggressive an your entry you chose.

I think some have been looking for the long here for awhile, and it may work. But keep in mind that same upper trend line will be there to offer resistance. And it has now been tested and confirmed, so we know its a good line. Maybe something to keep in mind when determining your TPs? And, if you do use that as a factor in setting your TP for along trade, keep in mind the degenerative effect of time on price, since its a downtrending line.

That is one reason I look for shorts at the outer, top TL of a downward sloping trend channel. Still wait for the same indicators for entry as well-discussed here. Even if that trend line line didnt hold, I would still be looking for it to retrace back down to that line (barring some intervening news release that may have altered the fundies, of course). If nothing else, that line will often work as support upon retrace.

As you can tell, I like trend channels. They are simple to use, offering both an easy visual of the trend in your timeframe, plus the same or similiar S/R characteristics as independently drawn trend lines. TCs also mesh very well with DAZ's method since they are both grounded in the use of swing highs/swing lows. They are part math, part art, but it doesnt take much practice to get a handle on them.

Just my 2 pips worth. Hope someone finds it useful.

The second chart is the CHF updated from above. If you recall, the idea was that price would return to the channel. Which it has for now.

--- 帖子 #999 ---
Hi Mike and dod:

It is really not complicated -- just parallel, equidistant lines. I can see how it might look like a fancy regression formula since that is what happens so often -- "price always returns to where its been."

The programer who gave me this neat little tool is the same one who did not give me the fib expansion tool  So there you go.

Anyway, its not that tough to do your own. Some trading software has a "copy line" feature. Just start on the top with at least two points on a downsloping trend, or at the bottom with two points for an uptrend. Copy that line and move it to the opposite swing h/l. Copy again, and stick that one in the middle (eyeballing is usually good enough). 3 lines suffice, you dont really need all 5 like mine shows. Make sense?

But dod is correct, the key is that it incorporates swing highs and lows. Thats why it works. In fact, it makes it easy to identify them. And it's the same reason why it meshes so well with DAZ' system.

Longer term works better. With the 60M, 4-5 days can be the start of a good one. Like everything else, its not 100%. Just one more tool for the toolbox. However, I find that once you have identified a good one, price will keep honoring it unless or until something shakes it out of the channel. I put them on all TFs. I try to pick a color that fades to the background so I can still see it but it doesnt dominate the landscape. Price should do that. If it fails, just delete it. Keep the ones that hold price.

Below is an example of what else you can do with it. Now we have a possible uptrending channel off the longer term downtrend on that EUR. Who will win this battle? Who knows. But have a look at the outer upper and lower lines which project a simple pattern shape (some type of triangle). One thing you find is that when these outer lines of opposite slope intersect, something usually happens with price, one way or the other. Sometimes, it just explodes out of there. I've always assumed it's because of the extra amount of stops and other orders that collide in that zone. Interesting? Since you are reading this thread, you probably think so, just like me

Maybe tommorrow I will really freak you out with a pitchfork to project price once it violates a TC. Dont laugh too hard, it can also be a handy little tool under the right conditions.

In the meantime, we'll see what happens, if anything, with this one.

Hi guys:

EUR 60m held at the upper line of the newer trend channel.

It is just a trend line after all.

Still, its helpful to have possible targets and/or reversal points clearly set out in advance.

Chart 1 -- price reaches upper line of upsloping trend channel. Where will price go next?

Chart 2 -- price retraces down to the upper line of previous downsloping trend channel. What was resistance, became support. Also at the 50 price level. Where will price go next?

Chart 3 -- here we insert the pitchfork I mentioned yesterday. Like the DAZ, it's drawn off swing points to project price into the future. The effectiveness of both depends most upon correctly identifying swing highs and lows. There is supposedly an 80% chance price will reach the median line if the swing high/low are correct.

Chart 4 -- price reaches median line.

Using the method of this thread plus these simple tools to establish S/R levels and price targets might have allowed a trader to capture a portion of each leg of the 1-2-3 or ABC.

Hi guys:

I have been reading about certain brokers raising what they charge for spreads; it has increased dramatically.

I have also been told of brokers that have changed their rollover rates policy practically overbight. Individuals that had gbp/jpy LONG are now paying interest instead of receiving. Other currency pairs have also been affected.

I use ODL, everything is still the same with them.

Alpari traders have been hit hard.

Please check your broker to see if you are affected.

To see this information for yourself, please go to the main page of Forex Factory. Go down to Trader Discussion and choose "Why I get negative interest when I have gbp/jpy LONG?"

Hi D liberators:

The indicator that Bee provided is a timer.

It lets you know how much time is left before the current candle closes.

It automatically recalculates when the timeframes are changed.

I find it very useful since this way I do not have to track exactly when I placed a trade.

I hope that this helps.

--- 帖子 #1116 ---
Hi Coobin:

I remember a discussion in the trading room a while back about individuals trading only certain pairs. The thing that stuck out to me back then was the reply by one of our veterans. He responded by stating that it did not matter to him what the currency pair was, a potentially good trade setup is a good setup no matters the pair.

Many comments have been made by various individuals that it is better to work with only a few pairs so that you can understand their individual behaviours. Before understanding fibonnacci, this seemed to be accurate to me. After learning fibonnacci, my personal feeling is that the emotions are no longer involved in my trading so I simply follow what the daz system and fibonnacci says I should do. to me, understanding the fibonnacci and Daz system is more important than understanding the behaviour of a pair.

Prior to the Daz system, I was trading only about six(6) pairs all USD, I was told that this was the best thing to do. Now, I trade a minimum of 15 pairs. This provides more chances of finding atleast one setup for the Daz system daily and sometimes none. It is more work reviewing each chart, but the results received are well worth it.

The comment made by one of our veterans in the trading room is what had me open up myself to other pairs. This has proven to be very helpful to my trading since I get more possibilities of a Daz setup.

Veterans, you just never know how you are affecting us new guys with your wisdom. Thank you guys, keep discussing.

Now, everything stated above is simply my personal opinion based on my personal experience so far which is less than a year.

The truth is, to be successful with this system or any system, we have to be good students. Decide that this is the system for you and delve into it. Read the thread numerous times, study every chart that is posted and most of all, get involved in actively trading(Keep it very small until you are comfortable, but get started).

Thanks again to everyone involved with keeping this thread alive and well.

--- 帖子 #1156 ---
EXIT STRATEGY

Carrying on from the previous example, I would exit my first lot at Target 1. If price does reach Target 2, I will take out the second lot, and move my stop loss to Break Even (Entry point). I will then take out my last lot when Target 3 is reached.

If you look at the charts provided, you can see that the targets can be calculated using the Fibonacci Expansion tool.

-When the confirmation candle is a Harami (Inside bar), use FE 50.0 as Target 1, FE 61.8 as Target 2 and FE 78.6 as Target 3.

-When the 'AB' wave consists of more than 10 candles, use FE 50.0 as Target 1, FE 61.8 as Target 2 and FE 78.6 as Target 3.

-When the confirmation candle is quite large, use FE 61.8 as Target 1, FE 78.6 as Target 2 and FE 100.0 as Target 3.

--- 帖子 #1157 ---
Hey Naijafx,

I got the exit strategy well, what I meant is with wich of the three targets you have to calculate that 1:1.5 ratio. The first one or the third one ?

Let's say my stop loss is at 100 pips, my first target at 50 pips and my third target at 150 pips. If I take the first target the ratio is 100:50 = 1:0.5 but if I take the third target now the ratio is 100:150 = 1:1.5 and the setup becomes valid. So that makes a big difference...

--- 帖子 #1230 ---
I’ve been trading a very similar system for the last couple of years with quite good results. I however use 61.8 – 76.4 fib levels and 10-3-3 low/high for my stochastic. I think that those who only look at 1 and 4 hour timeframes miss out on a lot of trades though because I take most of my trades off the 15 minute. I always look at the 1 and 4 hour for direction, but get in of candlestick patterns on the 15 minute charts, basically the CI System that’s found in Rob Moubray and Ken Marshall’s e-book, Guide to profitable forex day trading. Candlestick patterns off the 15 minute usually coincide with the 5/13 ema crossover so you could actually do a search in this forum and get one of those crossover indicators with an alert so every time the 5 and 13 ema cross the alert goes off and I just check my charts to see if it is a valid trade on the 15 minute. The downside of the alert is that when the market is going sideways it goes off all the time, but of course you don’t take those trades, just use the alert as an alert to check your charts. The other advantage of the 15 minute charts is that you don’t need as much of a stoploss as the swing low or swing high is smaller. Anyways, don’t discount the 15 minute, if you learn to trade it properly you wont get whipsawed at all. I also use a macd and look at Elliott waves as extra filters and am getting a very good win/loss ratio.

--- 帖子 #1236 ---
You were trading against divergence with that one. Look at the previous swing low on  6 Oct and the low on 10 Oct. When you get divergence like that you normally get an ABC correction, so look for a 3 wave correction before jumping on and as a guideline the anticipated target of the correction is the previous swing high, double top from 9 Oct. More importantly though you need the ABC correction. Always look at waves on degrees lower and 1 degree higher to the timeframe you are taking the trade off. I advice that you also throw on Bill William’s Awesome Oscillator or the standard MACD and then drag your stochastic over the top of it and then go to smaller timeframes before taking the trade. Never trade against the AO divergence until it has completed a correction. I would only have started looking for shorts on the eurusd after I had divergence on the AO on the 15 minute chart, and of course I would want a candlestick pattern and a resistance area such as a double top or trendline. Don’t take every setup, look at the bigger picture and take only the trades with more things going for it and you’ll find the win/loss ratio will improve.

--- 帖子 #1238 ---
I look at Elliott Waves and as you probably know the Elliott Wave Principle works on motive and corrective phases. The theory is that in an uptrend you have 5 waves up (numbered) and 3 waves down (lettered). And every wave has smaller subwaves within it, so for example wave 3 on the 1 hour will have 5 subwaves which can be easily spotted one degree lower (on the 15 minute chart). When wave 3 on the 1 hour is completed you will normally get divergence on the 15 minute chart which means you now will have an ABC correction so if I’m trading the 15 minute chart I wouldn’t be taking the next candlestick entry signal to go long, because more likely then not it is wave B. When wave B has finished you could trade wave C if you wanted to, but if you prefer to only take trades with the trend you would wait for wave C to complete and then trade wave 5 on the 1 hour which again should have 5 subwaves going up. It depends on how aggressive you are, you could enter wave 5 (on the 1 hour) off a candlestick pattern once you can see an ABC, remember to make sure that the ABC is complete otherwise you will jump in half way through wave 4 and of course you will get stopped out. I am more conservative and will wait for subwave 1 and 2 to complete and then jump in on subwave 3 of wave 5. Of course it’s not as simple as that because you often get wave extensions but after a while you can easily count the waves, and if you can’t, just leave that market alone and move to another currency. It’s a bit hard to explain but read this, and remember these aren’t true Elliott Waves, Elliott works on price alone, these are waves of momentum. They are however often the same as Elliott Waves only they don’t take the 3 rules of Elliott into account. It will however keep you out of trouble and give you a basic understanding of Elliott Waves. I don’t trade it strictly the way the manual says, I use candlestick patterns to enter my trades rather then a dma, and like I said, I look at price to mark my waves rather then momentum. I do however use the Awesome Oscillator for divergence at the end of wave 5 and want the oscillator to pull back to zero for wave 4 to be complete and then start looking for entries into wave 5. Remember to always look at subwaves though ALWAYS.

--- 帖子 #1239 ---
Forgot to mention… I take all my trades off the 15 minute chart but always look at the 1 and 4 hour. With the 15 minute I can use a very little stoploss and because I know what wave we should be going into on the higher degree, I can let my second contract run until subwaves tell me that it’s ready to pull back. And I only trade waves 3-5 and C of the 15 minute. That of course means that may trade wave A and 4 of the 1 hour, but only subwaves 3-5 and C within them. A bit hard to explain, so sorry if I’ve confused you.

Hey Mike.  I didn't know you were looking for me. We should chat again sometimes. I'll try  to elaborate. If you are really worried about newbies you should give them the  most important advise a veteran can give. And that is they should make the  trading system their own. No two traders are the same even if they follow the  same system. Boy I wish someone had given me this advice when I started out. It  would've saved me time and money both. We were fortunate enough to be part of  this system when dazfx originally posted it. We chatted with him in our trading  room and learned from him. Then he left and all of sudden people introduced this  indicator and that indicator and this new rule and that new rule and so on.  That's when I decided to bail out of this thread and the trading room. I learned  the hard way information overflow can kill you in this business.

Daz  introduced a simple way of trading and believe it or not it works. Each trader  can then adapt the method in a manner that fits his/her personality. For example  you discovered that drawing dynamic trendlines fit your trading style better and  that's perfectly all right. But that doesn't mean that it's the only way to look  for setups. It's just what you perceive as an optimal setup. I on the other hand  like to look for previous highs and lows and drop to a lower time frame and look  for setups. That doesn't mean my way is better than someone else's. It's just  how I see the market.

So when someone posts a question wondering why he  didn't see the setups you saw I tried to tell him to go back to the first page  and try to understand the basics and make this system work for his style of  trading and that's all.

Remember, you and I can follow the same system and  produce drastically different results. You can get rich and I can go broke and  that's the reality of trading. So don't take offense to what I say. The market  humbled me in the past but gave me the experience I needed to turn the corner  and if I can share my experience with a fellow trader I won't hesitate.

Take  care my friend.

Hello, the market moves in a wave form, and we trade the latest wave swing once the global trend is known. we have the impulsive wave(movement along the global trend) and the corrective wave(the pull back)

Take for Instance GBPUSD, the global trend(daily) is bearish, we go to one hour and look for bearish wave not more than 12 candles and wait for retracement, then trade accordingly as per the rule in the first page.

Hope your question has been answered sastifactory.

Mike

--- 帖子 #1285 ---
I have a question concerning the original Daz strategy. One of his entry rules states that:

"At the precise entry point ... on the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking up/down ..."

For those that have traded with this approach, and maybe discussed the issue, does this mean that the Stoch cross and hook:

1. Must have occurred at the close of the Confirmation Bar, and must also be evident at the moment of entry, which would be near the 5ma, which could be some way from the Confirmation Bar close.

2. Needn't have occurred at the close of the Confirmation candle but must be evident at the moment of entry, near the 5ma, which could be some way from the Confirmation Bar close.

If the answer is (1) then the Stoch cross would show up after the trade was over, and also in backtests; but if the answer is (2), then the Stoch could 'uncross' again prior to the entry bar closing.

I'm posting this in both 'Daz' threads ...

Now for sma5, all it does is to give u better entries, most times signal will be way off the sma5 when it comes, but since sma5 is known as a moving average that attract price, wot i do is to place PO close to the sma5 and go away. Happy new year all,

once in a while, i read daz post to refresh and i found this, it might help so much in trading the method

Hi David,

Its 12:33am here in the UK, but I will try my best to answer your questions.

1) The ideal setup is when the levels are touched to the pip, or when they are tested (candle close inside the levels). Then you have the setups where the candle is a few pips short of the levels. If you keep your AB waves short (4-10 candles) by moving to the appropriate TFs, you will be surprised at how often price respects these levels, especially when its moving with the longer term trend. Price could go beyond 78.6, but it should close below the level.

2) Yes, the hook up/down should happen either in the Confirmation Candle or the Entry Candle.

3) Looking back at my initial post, I can see I haven't made it very clear. Its Target 3.

4) When I first came up with this strategy, I moved stop to b/e upon hitting target 1. The problem with that is price will hit my entry point and continue moving in my direction taking out the other targets. This happens much frequently than price reversing at target 1.

5) 15/20 winning trades. 3/20 hit stop. 2/20 hit stop after hitting Target 1. All based on trades taken on the hourly time frame and mostly following the rules.

As you quite nicely said, this is just a ballpark idea, I don't want to mislead anyone.

Having said all this, the Entry, Exit rules are what I follow (My emotions do get the better of me sometimes) and not a requirement for this system to work effectively. I am sure there are better entry/exit strategies out there.

I hope I have answered your questions to your satisfaction.

-DAZ-

--- 帖子 #1349 ---
Daz stated tht we should look for set ups in the 'direction' of the bigger trend.

How u interprete the above statement matters.(this is where discretion comes in and why some find it difficult to trade this method i think)---

direction of the bigger trend implies the present direction and not necessarily the major trend.

What i'm trying to say is this if the major trend (impulse wave) on the daily is down (as in GU) but presently there's a clear retracement of the wave going on, i would prefer to trade lower tf in the direction of the daily retracement or better still stay out of the pair and wait for it to resume the direction of the impulse wave on the daily.

just my own 2 cents opinion.

--- 帖子 #1403 ---
hey paul - determining the trend is the hardest element of this strategy, when you get this right, everything else simply falls into place.

i personally do what Daz recommended - look at higher TF's.  Daz recommended looking at least 2 TFs higher (so Daily if you trade the 1HR).  And then simply looking at the way price is trending by looking for Higher Highs, Lower Lows etc

hope that helps

iffy

--- 帖子 #1405 ---
That's where discretion comes into play. Defining trend on daily tf totally depends on the look-back period, IMO. As an example I am attaching current GBPUSD daily chart. Now, B-C period can be defined as uptrend if your look-back period strats from B. But if your look-back period starts from A, then B-C can be defined as a retracement of a downtrend. So it is really a subjective issue.

--- 帖子 #1406 ---
For simplicity sake, you sell in 1hr time frame once the daily is making Lower low and Lower high and you buy 1hr time frame when daily is making higher high and higher low.

you will alwayz get at least a trade per day

--- 帖子 #1449 ---
I keep looking at these pictures and the fib start and end points, as far as I can tell, they're drawing them in the right direction however they do not consider market expansion or contraction so that their start or end are connected at the right place. In other words, if momentum (stoch) is overbought, we would consider a contraction is taking place and hook our fib line to start of the next swing low. Had this been done on a few of these trades, price would have hit the 78 and 61.8 perfectly, allowing for an earlier entry than the 5 sma. A quick look at the indicator at that point would confirm that a person was right in their selection.

--- 帖子 #1456 ---
The main thing is to look for the breakout of the 1 st wave after the retracement at fib level.This AMG wave tread as I said earlier is the attack of the 3rd or 5th Wave.Once you have identified the breakout as your entry, then take profit while you can just as the great Bernard Barouch would have approached it.The Fib extension level is a good way to exit, before a winning trade becomes a looser.

There are plenty of literature on EW in the net.I agree with naijafx.Say that you are an intraday trader and your fav TF is 1hr.You have to look where you are in the larger timeframe.In which elliot wave are you at the particular moment in a higher timeframe?You could be in a second wave in a 4hr TF etc.That itself could tell in which direction you are heading in relation to the EW of larger TF.Think about it.I hope that make sense.Hopefully I m allowed to post examples here...

Just stumbled across this thread and the method looks extremely interesting. The problem I have is im very inexperienced on MT4 and im not sure how to work out the extensions.

I can add the standard Fib retracements easily enough, but when I use the fib expansion tool on MT4 and draw a line from the swing high to the swing low or vice versa (point A to point B), the line that bounces off of this point doesnt reach the point "C" on the chart, as it appears to in the screenshots other people are showing.

I am assuming I am doing it right by plotting the fib extension from point A to point B, or should you move it around until the diagonal line that bounces off is at point C?

--- 帖子 #1567 ---
Doubleclick the dotted line of FE tool and you will get handles on all three ends. Then you can drag the C point to the right place.

There are some numbers somewhere in the first pages of this thread. If I remember correctly, Daz, originator of this system, was talking about 75% winners vs. 25% loosers (his own results). Which is very good.

If you are interested in this method, you should go through the whole thread. The method itself is really easy, figuring the trend direction is the hard part, but you will get some hints. There are several ways to aproach this problem.

Ultimately you have to find out for yourself, because results of other people may not apply to you. No two people are going to trade same setup same way (or even see the same setup, as you just witnessed), which is one may be winner and the second one looser.

Anyway, good luck.

--- 帖子 #1592 ---
LOL...... nice pic.Got to love that hook.Looks sharp.I bet it hook a lot of pips.LOL

Candle stick formation is PA( Price Action) and the stoch is for reference.Stoch is a lagging indicator.It tells the momentum of the movement but it does not tells us truely the direction is going to be.Price movement dictates the stoch.

--- 帖子 #1593 ---
Stoch set to 8,3,3 is quite fast, so if the confirmation candle is convincing enough, from what I have seen so far (I trade this only one week, still testing, so ...) it will hook on next candle after the confirmation candle more often then not - at least that's my limited impression. Propably somebody more experienced will step in here.

But it's fine to enter even if it hooks later, as long as your projected RRR is sound and price action is in your direction. RRR is likely to be sound if you are entering near SMA5. That means that if the price have moved to far from it and did not retraced a bit to give you better entry, you simply ignore the setup and move on.

The picture illustrates perfect entry: first it creates inverted hammer right above 78.6, first sign of reversal. Then it tests 78.6 and creates bullish candle. It also tests long term diagonal trendline and rejects it. Stoch crosses at the same time. It's pretty clear what's going on here, especially retrospectively

--- 帖子 #1594 ---
Right. I am happy to ignore stoch if I see high reliability candle reversal formation, but not the other way. I would not act on stoch alone, if the price action is not right.

--- 帖子 #1599 ---
Well, let me make the counterargument

As you can see on weekly, there is a hanging man at the end of an uptrend, and the price is going down from there. E.g. sign of consolidation and potential major correction on weekly graph. I would rather avoid trading with bulls with such setup.

On a daily graph you can see unfinished and imperfect falling three methods (ok, they are just two, but anyway), a high reliability continuation pattern. So it's down on daily two, at least if this pattern will hold, as it is not finished yet.

And finally, if you look at your graph, you will see big head and shoulders, also signaling down.

So the entry is valid, speaking technically, but against the trend, e.g. it's low propability trade.

I would skip it and do the same in opposite direction.

EDIT: another way to look at that daily pattern is bearish engulfing (in making), e.g. down.

--- 帖子 #1602 ---
Well, it always looks like a trend at the beginning of correction, right

There is major correction going on on S&P, which means dolar strenght and weekness for EUR and GBP. As investors are selling stocks, they are buying dollar (and carry traders JPY).

Here is a bigger picture:

Pic 1: SPX - correcting

Pic 2: USD index against other majors - this range is going on for a month and now it seems USD is breaking up (Pic 3, at least I hope, it has been pretty boring).

Pic 4: index of other majors against JPY - negatively correlating with S&P because of carry traders, JPY is going up.

Pic 5: GBP index, possibly starting correction, even though it still looks like an uptrend.

With JPY going up and GBP ranging or going down, direction of GBPJPY is pretty clear. With big correction on S&P I bet there is going to be correction on most majors, maybe not a big one, but for next week or two I would not go with previous trend. Too risky. It's possible to trade within the range, but you have to follow the candles and daily pattern on GBPJPY seems to be pretty bearish. Sure, the weekly pattern may turn into something else later this week, but I would not bet a lot on an uptrend. It will be correction down or more ranging. Tough times ahead.

Situation on GBPUSD is exactly the same.

--- 帖子 #1604 ---
hcristea, on the other hand, don't let my analysis mess up with your head. If you think you are right, go ahead. My trading improved significantly after I stopped reading analyses by other people, and especially after I stopped reading news with their "dollar lost xxx cents against euro because of [insert random reason here]".

I stopped with fundamental analysis after reading Nassim Taleb's book The Black Swan, which is about randomness. He mentions some research done by two researchers, who examined 27,000 predictions made by 300 "experts" in socioeconomical matters. They have found, that these experts can not predict anything better then average cab driver. Go figure

I only follow opinions of few professional traders, one of them being Hussin Naiji, who runs his own thread here at FF:

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=69786

The opinion about correction and downtrend is his and I agree based on my own candlestics analysis. As they say in his thread, never trade against Hussin  I understand the fallacy of argument by authority, but I have never seen him getting this wrong.

--- 帖子 #1605 ---
Just add the indicator(s) , modify the period as required, choose if you want  to see both normal and hidden divergence. |Then take the alerts with a 'pinch of salt'. That is, there is nothing that can 100% predict the future the best a good indicator or chart pattern can do is to give a higher probability of a move in one direction rather than the other.

If you are interested in divergence indicators, here are some that I have adapted (to remove delays and fix the problem of constant alerts when both normal and hidden divergence are triggered at the same time).

They are all originally based upon FX5's MACD divergence indicator, with modifications by SMJones (originally posted on the JAKONE thread).

They are not perfect since they miss divergences and alert for some very marginal divergences. I partucularly like the fact that they alert, because I don't want to spend all my time watching my charts.

Ian

--- 帖子 #1655 ---
Because there are no new trades to enter into, I will post few graphs and what I see regarding trend directions, because this method relies on them.

First is USD index against other major currencies. First on a weekly graph we can see five weeks long consolidation. On a daily we see that during these five weeks USD has been trading in upwards pointing triangle with no clean break through upper side. On H4 there was false break through lower trendline, but the price is now back in triangle. With S&P and other indexes dropping we should have expected strong dollar, so this long consolidation is likely effect of the interventions mentioned in previous post. I would expect more of this in comming days, maybe weeks. To get clear direction on USD we would need S&P going up (USD down), or central bankers to be overpowered by markets (USD up) - likely not gonna happen, as these people have quite a lot of money to pursue in their "interventions". Especially Brits tends to keep their currency strong at all costs, even if it kills British economy.

This makes trading USD crosses hard on longer timeframes, because they are in consolidation too. I always look at where USDLFX is headed intraday, and try to trade it against currency heading opposite side intraday, if there is good setup. Safest approach is to watch this situation from the sidelines and enter only into A trades.

--- 帖子 #1661 ---
Generally what I am trying to do in consolidation like this is to watch indexes on daily or H4 for candlestick formations giving me reversal signals, and then trying to trade pairs of currencies going in opposite directions (or one having direction and other one consolidating). I am taking either daz setups or bounces from S/R levels, with candlesticks giving me hints about directions. It's tricky, still learing, but getting there. Consolidations happen quite often, so I guess it's useful to learn how to trade through them without getting wiped out.

--- 帖子 #1740 ---
I thought I would share my twist on DAZfx's fib system. Nothing fancy, just better suited to my shorter term nature. Ive attached several charts for reference.

Following our run up this morning, my 195 tick (roughly = 5min) Macd crossed as price sold off. The ensuing rally took us right into the .618/.786 retrace area. I approach entry here by dropping down a multiple of 5 (to 39 tick chart, roughly = 1min). I have the 5SMA on this chart, as well as a weighted 5,3,8 Sto. The 8 smoothing helps with delaying the %K cross, as well as helping me pick off some even lower TF scalps (not addressed here). As the first chart shows, my 39tick peaked nicely as price rallied to our fib area, and then it closed down below its 5SMA. While aggressive, I prefer this type entry as the risk is smaller vs the potential reward.

I exited just beyond the .618 MM which was also a retest of the prior low.

We didnt reach the 1.00MM before price rallied again. This set up my 2nd short (see chart 2 of 39tick only). Once again, you can see the peak reached and the Sto's position, and its 5SMA being breached. I actually exited this position around the 30 level as I ran out of time.

I included one last chart of a later long (I was not here to trade this). After seeing the Macd cross and price rally, we pulled back on the 195tick. We pulled back just slightly beyond the .786 area, but the 39tick chart helped to defiine our long entry. We had a nice up candle breaching the 5SMA accompanying our Sto cross to trigger us in.

Perhaps someone will find this helpful in trading these fib setups. Thanks to DAZfx for the original disclosure of this nice approach to the markets. I have simply tweaked the entry methodology to fit my nature. Great trading to you!

Ninja

--- 帖子 #1741 ---
As price rallied this morning, my Macd crossed, and I highlited the .618/.786 retracement area looking for a possible pullback. Dropping down to my lower TF, I was watching for the Sto to reach OS within this retr area. The initial white candle triggered me, and I bought as price pulled back slightly. We retested on the 39tick, and as such I sat thru a few pips of heat. The Sto showed nice divergence on the retest. One thing Ive found on these entries is that we want to see that 5SMA turn in our favor soon after entry if not right then. I did have one last brief retest, and then off it went. Partial out at the .618MM, and balance at retest of high. Had I had one more contract on, I would hold it for the shot at the confluent 1.00MM/1.272extension area.

--- 帖子 #1742 ---

--- 帖子 #1743 ---
Hi.  I believe DAZfx counts the candles in the impulse wave (leg A of possible ABC) to estimate time duration of the C leg (move back in trend direction following correction) as a guideline to help with exits.  To date, I have focused on using the .618MM, prior pivot point (high/low), and 1.00MM/1.272extension area for exits.  To data, Ive not taken symmetry into acct so far for an exit guideline.  It is certainly a valid concept (I learned it from Borodyn's fib work), and one I intend to monitor.

--- 帖子 #1747 ---
Following the retest of the 9:30+ (eastern) high by the 10:30ish high, I highlited the .618/.786 retr area and waited to see if price pulled back here. On my entry chart, based upon the Sto crossing and positive candle, I got long on a small pullback following my trigger. This occurred around the top of the retr area. Price then moved down a bit more to reach (and briefly exceed) the .786 fib. During this time, note the %K on the 195 tick Sto. It was rising (diverging) and was crossing its %D. While I dont enter using this, it can provide insights to help with the smaller TF Sto timing. When I got the nice positive candle breaching the 5SMA on the 39 tick, I added on. At this point, I was less than 5 pips from B.E., and given the technical evidence, felt this was acceptable. While I dont recommend this to all, this is simply how I trade.

As I had to leave shortly, I exited as I hit the .618MM target (I tried to grab the chart right after I exited). I see price eventually reached the prior high as well.

This was certainly not a nice and neat "textbook" type setup, and this is why I wanted to post it. The size of the .618/.786 area dictates that we need to be flexible. And on this TF, its not nearly as large as a 1H or higher, and this is why I tend to stay on this lower TF. I can see more setups (albeit smaller targets), but with such a positive expectancy approach such as this, I want all the chances I can get! :-)

I hope you find something of value here.  Ive found that only by personalizing an approach to specifically fit each trader can he/she reap its full benefits (imho). Enjoy

--- 帖子 #1796 ---
I'd like to start by thanking Daz and by saying that I've been a long time lurker, but this has caused me to feel like posting.

I would like to share a few of my trades with this strategy from the last couple of days since I found this thread. I've done 5 trades total using this strategy and lost one (because I didn't follow the rules.. whoops  )

1) These were all live trades (on demo, using live data). Not backtest

2) I follow rules to a 'T', except for one which failed and hit my stop. I learned from that one

3) all trades were 1 std lot (aka $10/per pip)

Since this was a demo account, I thought I would also venture to see if this worked on lower TFs, as long as I follow the rules. All I can say is WOW.

I took 5 trades.

The 1st trade) Was on the hourly chart, which I lost big time on. I opened the trade a little early. I opened before Stoch "Hooked". The blue crossed the red, but it hadn't hooked yet, hitting my stop at about 25 pips back. 25 pips was within the 1.5:1 R/R, but at 3 lots, that hurts. I learned from that one. Oh, and it was with the trend, so I didn't play against the trend. Price just wasn't ready to go my way yet. A few candles later, it did. But I wasn't around to catch it that time.

The 2nd & 3rd trade) I couldn't find any setups at the moment to play with, so I opted to see if this would work on lower time frames. I tried on the 1m, using 15m as my trend guide. Following the rules closer this time (aka waiting for the "hook"), I got in and got out.  I hit all 3 targets and pulled 1 lot per. Now mind you it was only about 6 pips under 10 minutes, but @ 1std lot @ 10$/p using the 3 lot to start.. I believe it was just over 100$ trade. Not bad for 10 minutes work.  Both 1m trades were like this and totaled about 250$ work in trading. I attached one of the 1m trades. I didn't document the other.

The 4th trade) went back on the 1h chart. Played it perfect. With trend, hooked stoch, within the 61/78, etc. But I got scared. I didn't set my break even at the first target, but instead set it to about +2 pip when it was about half way to the first target. What happened? BOOM, hit my stop (not at a loss, but still). The trade ended up going all the way to target 3. Boy do I feel the fool. And it came NO WHERE near my original stop. It didn't even cross over my opening price. I wouldn't even have ever had to sweat this if I'd just kept my finger off the "freak out" trigger. See attached 1h chart for this blubber.

The 5th trade) I opted to find a happy medium while learning this strategy. 1m charts you have to be QUICK on. 1h -4h charts you have to have plenty of time to just mull over the charts to wait for the setups. So I looked at 30m charts using 4h as trend (2 TFs up). And NICE. Although I had to leave my desk to tend to the family, I just set my TP at the first target. I figured that's the bulk of the win, so I'd be happy. I check it later to see what it did, and it went all the way! See attached 30m chart.

All in all, these 5 trades gained about $4000 in 2 days, even with the loss of about 750$ (which shouldn't have happened if I'd been diligent), and considering I'm not adding any "what could have beens", for example my one trade I freaked out on and moved to BE early. Both of those losers could have been winners if I played by the rules, and then I would have had a REALLY good week.

I think I could live with that.  ........ **ponders where my compounding spreadsheet is****

Hope someone can use these examples for some good.

Hey Pip hows things.

To throw in my two pence worth, the setup looks fine to me. Although I prefer it when the stoch cross is well defined or obvious. I try to find an entry on or above the 5 sma when going short to get the best risk reward ratio I can, as the 5sma is only used for a guide to getting an optimum entry.

Also the trend on the daily chart in the short term is up ( previous month) and over the longer term bearish. Right now consolidating, if price were to fall below 143 and comtinue the longer term bear trend I would then be more comfortable looking to sell.

Hope that is useful VP

Did u look at H1 chart before entering? are u trend trader or counter trend?

Draw fibo on H1 chart to see where price bounce and go back? Draw two fibos on H1 to see on second one where price bounce? how much waves on H1 we have in up? answer to all these questions and u will get the right answer for u....

Never go against trend if u dont have 5years expirience in Forex trading..

Its not big deal. Keep it up, results will come.

Ps. Advice: always watch for trend on bigger timeframe, always try to go with trend and one more if u watch stoch and he is in overbought area and we have a up trend its not a signal for sell.... when we have up trend and have oversold area thats a signal for buy...

Good luck man

ok...lets start... in one trend how many waves we have? and how many corective waves? do u put on your chart pivot points, res and support lines?

If u are not shure on h1 is it up or down move switch to bigger tf and watch that chart... always unzoom to have a better view of price action....as u can see when u go short, price is testing a daily pivot , and she didnt close below that level, so enter is wrong... try to not be Nostradamus on Forex, try to play as price play.... second if u are not expirience so much to feel the trend put one or two moving averege....for evry position u need confirmation.... its never too late for 10-20pips, u learn on this things, later when u have more expirience u can play extremly , then u dont need confirmation.... third for me its most important when ever u see good setup, do some more reaserch take a look on H1, H4... big players make money on us, thats why when we go short they go long... so start to think like one of them, like u have so much money that u can move market and u always get profit.... discipline is also important, when u see that price break out trend dont hurry , she must go back again to test that new resistance line, if she close below new resistance then go short.... on stoch and macd look for convergence and divergence u can avoid bad signals if u use them for that...

I hope so some of this advice can help u.... if u are not confortable to trade alone pm me with your msn so u can always ask me what i think.... its always better to consultate with one or more guys becouse psyhology of human is greed , so are brain evry stupid candle see as entry signal, thats why u need patience and discipline.... and like my teacher say to me before one year psyhology is 80% of succes rest is elliot and fibs....

--- 帖子 #1893 ---
OK here is my analysis of the CHF JPY that led to the trade on the 4h chart, I am posting this hoping it is helpful to other people.

Weekly chart

Price had been moving in a sideways range breaking down out of the range on the 4th of Feb, after which a new low occured around the start of march. Then price put in a lower high on the 1st April.

Daily Chart

On the daily chart shown below this lower high happened at the top of an uptrend that lasted for a month through march. Then the daily made a lower high on the 15th of march and went on to break a lower trendline fitted to the uptrend.

4h Chart

As can be seen on the 4h chart I put in my previous post, price pulled back to the trendline and bounced off the 50sma and closed exactly on the 50% fib retracement. Also the CHFJPY and EUR JPY rallied far more weakly than the other yen currencies (Which were approaching the top of their recent trading ranges) in the final up move before the Daz trade triggered.

Happy trading people
