--- 帖子 #1935 ---
I have been reading the thread and am very impressed with the contributions most especially by Jhon and VP.

Let me cut in here before i give my insight to ur question. this system looks to trade a a daily trendy pair off 1hr TF as intra-day and 4hr as swing. trader's job is to look for a trendy pair on daily first and start trading in that trend on lower time frame

I will advice newbie to stay away from difficult pairs as it will lead to large drawdown. this system is one of the best on FF but it requires skills and experience to trade-in daily.

now to eurjpy:

Longtterm is bearish but presently there is strong contention between bear and bull, price is kinda consolidating on daily .

this pair is not good for this system now, it will take experienced trader who understand price action to trade eurjpy with this system with success with the on-going scenario on daily.

Note of warning again: i saw GCHF that VP took, though he admitted it was a counter trend, ofcourse it was but he was able to be smart enough to know when to bail out....... newbie, dont dare this approach, u will blow your acct.

My advice is look for trendy pairs. at times, u might not get a single trade using this system for weeks but u wont go broke trading it consistently.....

Hi

I marked what I think would be your ABC wave on the chart below. The only thing I would say about the ABC wave is it is very small (I think that is right as you have a long entry marked on your chart), with only one candle making up the BC wave and consequently no signal from the stock at the end of the BC part of the wave to give a point to enter. --- 帖子 #2004 ---
Hi and welcome to the thread. The trade may well work out well for you but if you are new to trading Daz setups it would be better to stay with the direction of the trend on the daily chart and avoid the more difficult counter trend setups, to increase the hit.  Also notice that yesterdays daily candle is pretty bearish and the trigger candle on the 4h and pryor candle do not make a bullish pattern. The trigger candle touched the high of the previos candle but only managed to close half way up the body.

Taking a setup where the candle pattern looks strong in the direction of the trade also is a factor to consider and will help increase the hit rate.

p.s My candle chart pattern looks slightly different to yours, only just noticed, different broker.

VP

--- 帖子 #2012 ---
Here is a nice tool (indicator) that draws the fibo levels with prices.

After you decide by yourself if the major trend is Long or Short, you change the trend in the indicator to show the pattern to TRUE and the opposite to FALSE.

I.e: if the trend is LONG, you change the SHORT option to FALSE.

"Draw SHORT pattern" = FALSE

TRUE is the default.

You also need to decide what is the minimum "range" of the move which you are looking to be retraced.

I don't understand why the problem with the Fibo drawing. If you draw from top to bottom the 100 is at the top, whereas if you draw from bottom to top the zero is at the top. In other words you start from the 100.

--- 帖子 #2023 ---
I am not VP but I will give my 2 cents.

You have 2 options:

a. Enter after the close of the first red bar (confirmation bar) and put your SL just above it. If your SL is hit, enter again after the next red bar.

b. Enter after the first red bar or even after the green bar (1 bar prior the red bar), and put your SL at the 78.6 fibo level.

--- 帖子 #2058 ---
Candle patterns.

Daz mentions this in the very first post to the thread and it makes a big difference, but it has not been mentioned much or discussed recently in the thread from what I have seen.

All other factors aside,  in this post I want to concentrate on specifically what is happening when price hits a Fib level, 50% , 62% or 78%.

Whichever Fib level it might be is not so important, unless it coincides with support or resistance but that is not what I want to talk about here. I want to focus in and look only for the moment  at the candle pattern.

What happens to candle pattern at the retracement level? Sure price might well bounce off as some sellers or buyers eye that point (50% , 62% or 78%) to enter postions. The stochastic (8,3,3) may also be crossing at whichever level as price bounces from the retracement level. The question is when you are looking at the chart, what represents a good opportunity?

Ok the following candle patterns will give better opportunities in my humble opinion.

First off and the most  powerful is this pattern. The candle before the trigger candle makes a new high. The trigger candle hits the high but does not breach it then goes on to close lower. A++ for me this is my favorite candle bounce off a fib level.

--- 帖子 #2059 ---
Next two I consider equal.

The first candle makes  a swing high and the next candle (signal candle ) falls straight back down and closes right on the open of the previous candle, this affectivly is a pin (extended over 2hours if it is seen on a 1h time frame for example). A Pin on the time frame of the trade is also just as good.

--- 帖子 #2060 ---
Next is this pattarn, which on a lower time frame would be a double bottom. The third candle in the circle needing to close at least as high as the first candle to complete the double bottom, but that is a perfect formation.

These three patterns form often on the charts at bounces from fib levels but they obviously are never perfect, approximations and judgements along with all other factors will make the trade.

--- 帖子 #2065 ---
Regarding your question about entry in gbpjpy:

In Dazfx's definition, or the following discussion, he defined the swing as approx 4-11 candles. If there where more candles then one should check the higer timeframe. In your case there are 17 candles, so H4 might be a better choice.

For the entry point he defined the reward:risk>=1.5. If I have understood this correctly then your entry should be between 0 and 31.44 when the last target is 78.6. This is what I call Entry Limit in my charts.

If all this is correct, then the candle after the second confirmation candle after point 1 is a legal entry. You will also have a legal entry at 2 after the confirmation candle.

Dazfx also emphasized the importance of not taking the entire swing. My proposal is shown having a swing of 7 candles.

--- 帖子 #2078 ---
Thanks for the reply.

My interest in this trade is mainly because the system use few indicators, is well defined (although I still have questions), and yours and vincentprices charts and comments are very helpfull and shows that it works.

I have never seen Dazfx explain how to calculate the risk reward.

If I ignore the spread and number of units/lots I trade, place stop loss at 0%, enter at 31.44% my risk is 31.44%. If the last profit target is 78.6% then (78.6-31.44)=1.5*31.44. That is: reward=1.5*risk.

Entering the trade before 31.44% will ofcourse improve the reward:risk ratio. If the last take profit level is 100%, then I should not enter after 40%.

How are you calculating the risk reward ratio?

--- 帖子 #2079 ---
Use stop just above point C.

I mostly use 1:1 for half lot size and 1:2 for remaining lot.

Here is method part from DAZ fx about profit targets.

EXIT STRATEGY

Carrying on from the previous example, I would exit my  first lot at Target 1. If price does reach Target 2, I will take out the  second lot, and move my stop loss to Break Even (Entry point). I will  then take out my last lot when Target 3 is reached.

If you look at the charts provided, you can see that the  targets can be calculated using the Fibonacci Expansion tool.

-When the confirmation candle is a Harami (Inside bar),  use FE 50.0 as Target 1, FE 61.8 as Target 2 and FE 78.6 as Target 3.

-When the 'AB' wave consists of  more than 10 candles, use FE 50.0 as Target 1, FE  61.8 as Target 2 and FE 78.6 as Target 3.

-When the confirmation candle is quite large, use FE 61.8  as Target 1, FE 78.6 as Target 2 and FE 100.0 as Target 3.

--- 帖子 #2080 ---
Yes. I know this, and try too follow it.
But it does not explain how too calculate the reward:risk ratio, which Dazfx say should be at least 1.5.

Referring to the same document as you , go to INVALID SETUPS point 2) which states:

2) If the confirmation candle moves so much that the stop loss is widened to a point where the Risk/Reward ratio is no longer 1:1.5.

Dazfx never explain how to verify/calculate Risk/Reward.

From your answer I see that my previous post might have mislead you since I did not emphasize that my procentages was FE procentages. In my previous post the 0% is Point C. So all my calculations refer too the expansion from retracement point C.

My calculations means that if I enter after FE 31.44% then the stop loss has widened to a point where my risk/reward is no longer 1:1.5.

In the STOP LOSS section of the same document, Dazfx states that

"Only take a trade if the stop loss is smaller than your projected target 2".

The STOP LOSS section actually says that if my second profit target is FE 61.8% then I should not enter a trade below 61.8%/2=30.9%.

I normally place stop loss a few pips behind point C. But I ignore these pips here because I want to keep it simple. I just need a visible rule of thumb for the Reward/Risk ratio.

--- 帖子 #2100 ---
Hey guys , refer to this post on the thread and section surrounding it for more information on trading off the 50% Fib level, is part of the Daz method using a few additional rules.

Advanced entry rules are stated below

1. Pull back to 38 or 50 fibo area

2. confirmation candle formed at either of the fibo number

3. sma(5) to give u good entry

4. stoch has crossed as usual

5. hidden divergence seen on stoch(hidden divergence indicates trend continuation)

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...=75922&page=45

--- 帖子 #2268 ---
Hi khalidhassan

Here the rules  by DAZfx

Long

Generally, you are buying in an uptrend, when the AB impulse wave retraces to the 61.8 or 78.6 level. Before pinpointing a precise entry, you wait for the next candle (confirmation candle) to form. This must not exceed the low made by the retracement and has to be a bullish reversal candle (ie, Harami, Doji, Bullish Maribozu, Bullish Belt hold, etc).

At the precise entry point:

1) The new candle following the Confirmation Candle is on or near the 5 SMA.

2) On the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking up. This cross should not happen in the overbought region (80 or above).

Short

Generally, you are selling in a downtrend, when the AB impulse wave retraces to the 61.8 or 78.6 level. Before pinpointing a precise entry, you wait for the next candle (confirmation candle) to form. This must not exceed the high made by the retracement and has to be a bearish reversal candle (ie, Harami, Doji, Bearish Maribozu, Bearish Belt hold, etc).

At the precise entry point:

1) The new candle following the Confirmation Candle is on or near the 5 SMA.

2) On the Stochastic Oscillator window, the fast stoch (blue line) has already crossed or is crossing the slow stoch (red dotted line) and hooking down. This cross should not happen in the oversold region (20 or below).

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Price dictates EVERYTHING - BUT you can certainly use Indicators to pick out turns - I've been doing it for decades

Once you get those big ranging bars, I'm not Interested in trading them, as its too risky, but on the way up to those big ranged bars you can definitely trade

The Indicators are cycle Indicators, as in they follow price action cycles, but you can use them to get in near the low bars of turns - trade with the trend though that is the critical part

--- 帖子 #2361 ---
I'm conscious of going off the original topic, but I was hoping to ask you what confirmations you look for on your method? I'm assuming its rejection off a MA and the RSI/ stoch bending upwards for a long entry or downwards for a short entry? Thank you in advance

--- 帖子 #2362 ---
Yeah - It's exactly as you'd use the stoch in the method in this thread - stochs RSI Indicators will all turn when a price cycle turns - that's all you're doing is catching the price cycle turn, it can be at a moving average, at a fib level, at a elliott wave count etc

If you look at the chart above - as soon as the 2RSI is <25% I'm on alert, to enter, price HAS to trade ABOVE the bar high of the bar that made the 2RSI go <25%, then if it does, I go long and the stop goes 1 penny under the LOW of the entry bar or the low of the bar which made the 2RSI go <25% whichever is lower and then I either set a price target or most often trail up a stop below the lows etc

You can be this precise, because if the Indicator is tracking price turns (as it does) then you can have confidence that your Initial stop will not be hit IF you have got the price cycle correct - If you apply this in a trendless market, then you will get kicked to hell as you would do if you just bought when the 2RSI goes <25% - so you need a few factors to happen to get in a position, exactly as you do at a fib level

IF the level you are trading is valid then price will move, if you've got it wrong, you'll get stopped - I used to trade fib levels with this method which is obviously counter trend

You can just trade the RSI or the STOCH on its own or you can use a combo of both i.e. only take trades when the trend is bullish and both the Indicators are oversold <25% or whatever

The Important factor is whatever Indicator you use, it WILL turn when the price cycle turns and as you can visually see, the Indicators catch a lot of the price cycle turns - there's no magic to this, price is always king, but it does very predictable things - When you trade Fib levels you'll find that sometimes the Indicator catches the turn perfectly and other times its wrong and price falls to another level etc, but when price is at the point of support and its going to turn, then the Indicator will follow suit

and by using the Indicator you can get in very very close to the low bar (for longs)

If you read those books, you will see that those 2 traders did this very thing at fib levels and with Indicators - the principle of this thread is THEIR methods - I've just applied it to another method I personally prefer

This is a recent one I saved - entry/stop and trail

I was also in on the 2 trades (not marked) in APRIL - one of which you can see would have been a FIB level reversal of some kind, but I wasn't trading the fib level, just the moving averages - so this should help to explain how it all fits together
